Update - Recent gcc version spacewalk error on 'make'  - The Fix

You may get the following error when trying to do the make step of the wifi backport as shown below.

[root@localhost backports-4.4.2-1]# make

make[5]: `conf' is up to date.

boolean symbol HWMON tested for 'm'? test forced to 'n'

boolean symbol HWMON tested for 'm'? test forced to 'n'

#

# configuration written to .config

#

Building backport-include/backport/autoconf.h ... done.

CC [M] /home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/main.o

CC [M] /home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.o

/home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.c:14:28: error: static declaration of ‘scatterwalk_ffwd’ follows non-static declaration

static struct scatterlist *scatterwalk_ffwd(struct scatterlist dst[2],

^

In file included from /home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.c:11:0:

include/crypto/scatterwalk.h:105:21: note: previous declaration of ‘scatterwalk_ffwd’ was here

struct scatterlist *scatterwalk_ffwd(struct scatterlist dst[2],

^

make[6]: *** [/home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.o] Error 1

make[5]: *** [/home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat] Error 2

make[4]: *** [_module_/home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1] Error 2

make[3]: *** [modules] Error 2

make[2]: *** [modules] Error 2

make[1]: *** [modules] Error 2

make: *** [default] Error 2

[root@localhost backports-4.4.2-1]# which gcc

/bin/gcc

[root@localhost backports-4.4.2-1]# gcc -v

Using built-in specs.

COLLECT_GCC=gcc

COLLECT_LTO_WRAPPER=/usr/libexec/gcc/x86_64-redhat-linux/4.8.5/lto-wrapper

Target: x86_64-redhat-linux

Configured with: ../configure --prefix=/usr --mandir=/usr/share/man --infodir=/usr/share/info --with-bugurl=http://bugzilla.redhat.com/bugzilla --enable-bootstrap --enable-shared --enable-threads=posix --enable-checking=release --with-system-zlib --enable-__cxa_atexit --disable-libunwind-exceptions --enable-gnu-unique-object --enable-linker-build-id --with-linker-hash-style=gnu --enable-languages=c,c++,objc,obj-c++,java,fortran,ada,go,lto --enable-plugin --enable-initfini-array --disable-libgcj --with-isl=/builddir/build/BUILD/gcc-4.8.5-20150702/obj-x86_64-redhat-linux/isl-install --with-cloog=/builddir/build/BUILD/gcc-4.8.5-20150702/obj-x86_64-redhat-linux/cloog-install --enable-gnu-indirect-function --with-tune=generic --with-arch_32=x86-64 --build=x86_64-redhat-linux

Thread model: posix

gcc version 4.8.5 20150623 (Red Hat 4.8.5-11) (GCC)

If you get this error, you need to edit the following file in the backport directory, and remove the word 'static' on line 14 as indicated by the error code:

/home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.c:14:28: error: static declaration of ‘scatterwalk_ffwd’ follows non-static declaration

Therefore edit the file as shown below, then run 'make defconfig-iwlwifi' per usual procedure,  and then run make per usual procedure.  This apparently has something to do with stricter checking in recent versions of gcc compiler.

root@localhost backports-4.4.2-1]# vi /home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.c

[root@localhost backports-4.4.2-1]# head -20 /home/ubuntu/Downloads/backports-4.4.2-1/compat/backport-4.2.c

/*

* Copyright (c) 2015 Hauke Mehrtens <hauke@hauke-m.de>

*

* Backport functionality introduced in Linux 4.2.

*

* This program is free software; you can redistribute it and/or modify

* it under the terms of the GNU General Public License version 2 as

* published by the Free Software Foundation.

*/


#include <crypto/scatterwalk.h>

#include <crypto/aead.h>


static struct scatterlist *scatterwalk_ffwd(struct scatterlist dst[2],  <-- Remove word 'static' at start of this line, save, then proceed with usual procedure.

struct scatterlist *src,

unsigned int len)

{

for (;;) {

if (!len)

return src;

[root@localhost backports-4.4.2-1]#

Update - Updating UEK4 Kernel Breaks Wireless Support - The Fix

An update to Oracle Linux 7 UEK4 kernel was waiting to ambush me this morning (October 12, 2016).  Being a serial fearless update-applier I boldly forged ahead.  And yup it broke Intel 8260 wireless support for the Lenovo P70 Mobile Workstation.  No matter.  Fortunately the backport can be applied again.  The good news is that I refined this procedure a bit and of course finally noticed that you only need to run "defconfig-iwlwifi" not the entire "defconfig-wifi" which is much quicker 2 or 3 minute operation to restore onboot wireless support for UEK4.  So, good morning UEK 4.1.12-61.1.13.el7uek.x86_64 and welcome to the team!

IMPORTANT NOTE:  The following steps have to be done when you are booted into the UEK4 kernel!  You have to download all the stuff you need when you are booted into the Oracle RedHat Compatible Kernel (which comes with the Oracle Linux distribution) because wired and wireless networking both work out of the box on that kernel on the Lenovo P70 mobile workstation.  Once you have downloaded the backports, installed required headers (for the UEK4 kernel!) then reboot into the UEK4 kernel and run the below.

[root@ol72 backports-4.4.2-1]# make defconfig-iwlwifi
Generating local configuration database from kernel ... done.
make[2]: `conf' is up to date.
boolean symbol HWMON tested for 'm'? test forced to 'n'
boolean symbol HWMON tested for 'm'? test forced to 'n'
#
# configuration written to .config
#
[root@ol72 backports-4.4.2-1]# make
make[5]: `conf' is up to date.
boolean symbol HWMON tested for 'm'? test forced to 'n'
boolean symbol HWMON tested for 'm'? test forced to 'n'
#
# configuration written to .config
#
Building backport-include/backport/autoconf.h ... done.

[root@ol72 backports-4.4.2-1]#

Summary

Today I set out to configure wireless on Oracle Linux UEK4 kernel and "...all day long the noise of battle roll'd among the mountains by the winter sea".  I'll add more details later, but the solution was found, in a place most unexpected, in a Linux Mint forum here and the solution is attributed to poster "Jeremy".  Thanks Jeremy.  Thanks.

I had done just about everything today trying to get this to work.  I actually recompiled the UEK4 kernel (successfully) with the wireless firmware etc. to no avail.  I thought this effort was a lost cause for today and perhaps for eternity.

I booted into my Ubuntu 16.04 where the wireless hardware driver loads up just fine and did a last minute fish on some output from dmesg | grep iwl there on Ubuntu and hit on the above referenced blog post.  The steps are really very simple basically.  They are listed below.

First you download the backport noted by Jeremy at the mint forum.  I've uploaded it to my blog here just so it never gets lost, because frankly, this was just a hail-mary attempt at the last minute.  It was a hail-mary backport that just happened to work.  Run the following as root user as shown below.

tar -zxvf backports-4.4.2-1.tar.gz
cd backports-4.4.2-1/
make defconfig-wifi
make
make install
reboot

On reboot, you should have wifi (see screenshot below). My guess is that this fix should work on any Lenovo ThinkPad with the 8260 network controller (see below to check for your controller version).

Procedure

Here are the detail screen outputs as shown below.  NOTE; For completeness this is the procedure below I actually used and I like to be historically accurate procedures being what they are and all (i.e. when curing cancer, it doesn't matter what you think you did, or what you thought you should have done, but rather, what you actually did, which can be devilish hard to recall) but see note above that you probably can just use "defconfig-iwlwifi" in what follows below instead of the full "defconfig-wifi" because all that is needed for this purpose are the iwlwifi backports.
